      <p>
       <b>
        Romansh
       </b>
       (also spelled
       <b>
        Romansch
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        Rumantsch,
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        Romanche
       </b>
       ; Romansh:
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-rumantsch.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/Roh-vallader-rumantsch.ogg" title="Roh-vallader-rumantsch.ogg">
          <i>
           rumantsch
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-rumantsch.ogg" title="File:Roh-vallader-rumantsch.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        rumàntsch
       </i>
       ,
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-rumauntsch.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c5/Roh-put%C3%A8r-rumauntsch.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-rumauntsch.ogg">
          <i>
           romauntsch
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-rumauntsch.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-rumauntsch.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-Sursilvan-Romontsch.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Roh-Sursilvan-Romontsch.ogg" title="Roh-Sursilvan-Romontsch.ogg">
          <i>
           romontsch
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-Sursilvan-Romontsch.ogg" title="File:Roh-Sursilvan-Romontsch.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance language
       </a>
       spoken predominantly in the southeastern
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Swiss
       </a>
       canton of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graub%C3%BCnden" title="Graubünden">
        Grisons
       </a>
       (Graubünden), where it has
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official status
       </a>
       alongside German and Italian. It is used as the medium of instruction in schools in Romansh-speaking areas. Romansh has also been recognized as a national
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Switzerland" title="Languages of Switzerland">
        language of Switzerland
       </a>
       since 1938, and as an official language since 1996, along with
       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Standard_German" title="Swiss Standard German">
        German
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       . It is sometimes grouped by linguists with
       <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
        Ladin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Friulian_language" title="Friulian language">
        Friulian
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/Rhaeto-Romance_languages" title="Rhaeto-Romance languages">
        Rhaeto-Romance language
       </a>
       , though this is disputed.
      </p>
      <p>
       Romansh is a descendant of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        spoken Latin language
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , which by the 5th century AD replaced the
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raetic_language" title="Raetic language">
        Raetic
       </a>
       languages previously spoken in the area. Romansh retains a small number of words from these languages. Romansh has also been strongly influenced by German in vocabulary and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morphosyntax" title="Morphosyntax">
        morphosyntax
       </a>
       . The language gradually retreated to its current area over the centuries, being replaced in other areas by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alemannic_language" title="Alemannic language">
        Alemannic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">
        Bavarian
       </a>
       dialects. The earliest writing identified as Romansh dates from the 10th or 11th century, although major works did not appear until the 16th century, when several regional written varieties began to develop. During the 19th century the area where the language was spoken declined, but the Romansh speakers had a literary revival and started a language movement dedicated to halting the decline of the language.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 2000 Swiss census, 35,095 people (of whom 27,038 live in the canton of
       <a href="/wiki/Grisons" title="Grisons">
        Grisons
       </a>
       ) indicated Romansh as the language of "best command", and 61,815 as a "regularly spoken" language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, Switzerland switched to a yearly system of assessment that uses a combination of
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Switzerland" title="Municipalities of Switzerland">
        municipal
       </a>
       citizen records and a limited number of surveys.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Based on this yearly system, the number of people aged 15 and above reporting Romansh as their main language was 36,622 in 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Office_fédéral_de_la_statistique_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Office_fédéral_de_la_statistique-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spoken by around 0.9% of Switzerland's 7.7 million inhabitants, Romansh is Switzerland's least-used national language in terms of number of speakers and ranks eleventh in terms of most spoken languages in Switzerland overall.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gross_2004._p._35_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gross_2004._p._35-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The language area and number of speakers of Romansh have been continually shrinking, though language use remains vigorous in certain areas.
      </p>
      <p>
       Romansh is divided into five different regional dialects (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sursilvan" title="Sursilvan">
        Sursilvan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sutsilvan" title="Sutsilvan">
        Sutsilvan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surmiran" title="Surmiran">
        Surmiran
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Put%C3%A8r" title="Putèr">
        Putèr
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vallader" title="Vallader">
        Vallader
       </a>
       ), each with its own standardized written language. In addition, a pan-regional variety called
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rumantsch_Grischun" title="Rumantsch Grischun">
        Rumantsch Grischun
       </a>
       was introduced in 1982, which is controversial among Romansh speakers.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>
