      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistic_classification">
        Linguistic classification
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romansh_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Linguistic classification">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Romansh is a
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance language
       </a>
       descending from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       , the spoken language of the Roman Empire. Within the Romance languages, Romansh stands out because of its peripheral location, which has resulted in several archaic features. Another distinguishing feature is the centuries-long
       <a href="/wiki/Language_contact" title="Language contact">
        language contact
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       , which is most noticeable in the vocabulary and to a lesser extent the syntax of Romansh. Romansh belongs to the
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
        Gallo-Romance
       </a>
       branch of the Romance languages, which includes languages such as
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
        Occitan
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Lombard_language" title="Lombard language">
        Lombard
       </a>
       . The main feature placing Romansh within the Gallo-Romance languages is the
       <a href="/wiki/I-mutation" title="I-mutation">
        fronting
       </a>
       of Latin
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">
         u
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Close_front_rounded_vowel" title="Close front rounded vowel">
         y
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">
         i
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       , as seen in Latin
       <i>
        muru(m)
       </i>
       'wall', which is
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-m%C3%BCr.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1e/Roh-put%C3%A8r-m%C3%BCr.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-mür.ogg">
          <i>
           mür
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-m%C3%BCr.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-mür.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg" title="Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg">
          <i>
           mir
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg" title="File:Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       in Romansh.
      </p>
      <p>
       The main features distinguishing Romansh from the
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Italic_languages" title="Gallo-Italic languages">
        Gallo-Italic languages
       </a>
       to the south are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(sound_change)" title="Palatalization (sound change)">
         Palatalization
        </a>
        of Latin K and G in front of A, as in Latin
        <i>
         canem
        </i>
        'dog', which is
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-tgaun.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/Roh-sursilvan-tgaun.ogg" title="Roh-sursilvan-tgaun.ogg">
           <i>
            tgaun
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
         <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            help
           </span>
          </a>
          ·
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-tgaun.ogg" title="File:Roh-sursilvan-tgaun.ogg">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            info
           </span>
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </span>
        in Sursilvan,
        <i>
         tgang
        </i>
        in Surmiran, and
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-chaun.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Roh-put%C3%A8r-chaun.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-chaun.ogg">
           <i>
            chaun
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
         <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            help
           </span>
          </a>
          ·
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-chaun.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-chaun.ogg">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            info
           </span>
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </span>
        in Putèr and Vallader (the difference between ⟨tg⟩ and ⟨ch⟩ being purely orthographic, as both represent /tɕ/). This sound change is partially absent in some varieties of Romansh, however, especially in Sursilvan, where it may have been reversed at some point: Sursilvan
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg" title="Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg">
           <i>
            casa
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
         <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            help
           </span>
          </a>
          ·
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg" title="File:Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            info
           </span>
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </span>
        and Vallader
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg" title="Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg">
           <i>
            chasa
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
         <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            help
           </span>
          </a>
          ·
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg" title="File:Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            info
           </span>
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </span>
        'house'.
       </li>
       <li>
        Pluralisation with "-s" suffix, derived from the
        <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
         Latin
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">
         Accusative case
        </a>
        , as in
        <i>
         buns chavals
        </i>
        'good horses' as opposed to Italian
        <i>
         buoni cavalli
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Retention of L following
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /p b k ɡ f/
        </span>
        : Latin
        <i>
         clavem
        </i>
        'key' &gt;
        <i>
         clav
        </i>
        as opposed to Italian
        <i>
         chiave
        </i>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
         <a href="#cite_note-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Another defining feature of the Romansh language is the use of unstressed vowels. All unstressed vowels (except /a/) disappeared.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1300" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png/220px-Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png/330px-Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png/440px-Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhaeto-Romance_languages.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The three proposed Rhaeto-Romance languages Romansh, Ladin, and Friulan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Whether or not Romansh,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friulan_language" title="Friulan language">
        Friulan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
        Ladin
       </a>
       should compose a separate "
       <a href="/wiki/Rhaeto-Romance_languages" title="Rhaeto-Romance languages">
        Rhaeto-Romance
       </a>
       " subgroup within Gallo-Romance is an unresolved issue, known as the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Questione_ladina" title="Questione ladina">
         Questione ladina
        </a>
       </i>
       . Some linguists posit that these languages are descended from a common language, which was fractured geographically through the spread of German and Italian. The Italian linguist
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graziadio_Ascoli" title="Graziadio Ascoli">
        Graziadio Ascoli
       </a>
       first made the claim in 1873.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The other position holds that any similarities between these three languages can be explained through their relative geographic isolation, which shielded them from certain linguistic changes. By contrast, the Gallo-Italic varieties of
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Italy" title="Northern Italy">
        Northern Italy
       </a>
       were more open to linguistic influences from the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">
        South
       </a>
       . Linguists who take this position often point out that the similarities between the languages are comparatively few.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This position was first introduced by the Italian dialectologist
       <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Battisti" title="Carlo Battisti">
        Carlo Battisti
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       This linguistic dispute became politically relevant for the
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_irredentism" title="Italian irredentism">
        Italian irredentist
       </a>
       movement. Italian nationalists interpreted Battisti's hypothesis as implying that Romansh, Friulan and Ladin were not separate languages but rather Italian dialects. They used this as an argument to claim the territories for Italy where these languages were spoken.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From a sociolinguistic perspective, however, this question is largely irrelevant. The speakers of Romansh have always identified as speaking a language distinct from both Italian and other Romance varieties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">
        Dialects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romansh_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Dialects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5240" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png/220px-Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png/330px-Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png/440px-Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Languages_and_dialects_of_Grisons.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Historical distribution of the dialects of Romansh, German, and Italian in Grisons. It should be noted that so-called "Italian dialects" are in fact dialects of Lombard, and more similar to Romansh than to Italian:
         <br/>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ED1C24; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Sursilvan
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF8080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Tuatschin
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #800040; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Sutsilvan
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Surmiran
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0080FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Putèr
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Vallader
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000064; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Jauer
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Romansh comprises a group of closely related
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">
        dialects
       </a>
       , which are most commonly divided into five different varieties, each of which has developed a standardized form. These standardized regional standards are referred to as
       <i>
        idioms
       </i>
       in Romansh to distinguish them from the local vernaculars, which are referred to as
       <i>
        dialects
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These dialects form a
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
        dialect continuum
       </a>
       without clear-cut divisions. Historically a continuous speech area, this continuum has now been ruptured by the spread of German, so that Romansh is now geographically divided into at least two non-adjacent parts.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         1.
        </b>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sursilvan" title="Sursilvan">
          Sursilvan
         </a>
        </i>
        (rm.
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-Sursilvan-Sursilvan.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/Roh-Sursilvan-Sursilvan.ogg" title="Roh-Sursilvan-Sursilvan.ogg">
           <i>
            sursilvan
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
         <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            help
           </span>
          </a>
          ·
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-Sursilvan-Sursilvan.ogg" title="File:Roh-Sursilvan-Sursilvan.ogg">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            info
           </span>
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </span>
        ; derived from the name of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surselva" title="Surselva">
         Surselva
        </a>
        -region, which itself is derived from
        <i>
         sur
        </i>
        'above' and
        <i>
         selva
        </i>
        'forest') – spoken in the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surselva" title="Surselva">
         Vorderrhein
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         Rain anteriur
        </i>
        ) valley, including the
        <a href="/wiki/Lumnezia" title="Lumnezia">
         Lumnezia
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Foppa" title="Foppa">
         Foppa
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Cadi_(Swiss_region)" title="Cadi (Swiss region)">
         Cadi
        </a>
        . It is the most widely spoken variety, with 17,897 people within the Surselva region (54.8%) naming Romansh as a habitually spoken language in the Swiss census of 2000.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gross31_14-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gross31-14">
          [14]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <b>
         2.
        </b>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sutsilvan" title="Sutsilvan">
          Sutsilvan
         </a>
        </i>
        (derived from
        <i>
         sut
        </i>
        'below' and
        <i>
         selva
        </i>
        'forest') – spoken in the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hinterrhein_(district)" title="Hinterrhein (district)">
         Hinterrhein
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         Rain posteriur
        </i>
        ) valley, including
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Imboden_(Bezirk)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Imboden (Bezirk) (page does not exist)">
         Plaun
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Heinzenberg_GR" title="Heinzenberg GR">
         Heinzenberg
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domleschg_valley" title="Domleschg valley">
         Domleschg
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Schams" title="Schams">
         Schams
        </a>
        . It is the least widely spoken Romansh variety, with 1,111 people within its historical area (15.4%) naming Romansh as a habitually spoken language.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gross31_14-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gross31-14">
          [14]
         </a>
        </sup>
        It has become extinct across much of its historical area since the turn of the 20th century.
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <b>
         3.
        </b>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surmiran" title="Surmiran">
          Surmiran
         </a>
        </i>
        (derived from
        <i>
         sur
        </i>
        'above' and
        <i>
         meir
        </i>
        'wall') – spoken in the
        <a href="/wiki/Gelgia_(river)" title="Gelgia (river)">
         Gelgia
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Albula_(river)" title="Albula (river)">
         Albula
        </a>
        valleys, including
        <a href="/wiki/Surses" title="Surses">
         Surses
        </a>
        and
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sutses&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sutses (page does not exist)">
         Sutses
        </a>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <b>
         4.
        </b>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Put%C3%A8r" title="Putèr">
          Putèr
         </a>
        </i>
        (rm.
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-put%C3%A8r.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Roh-put%C3%A8r-put%C3%A8r.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-putèr.ogg">
           <i>
            putèr
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
         <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            help
           </span>
          </a>
          ·
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-put%C3%A8r.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-putèr.ogg">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            info
           </span>
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </span>
        ; probably originally a nickname derived from
        <i>
         put
        </i>
        'porridge', meaning 'porridge-eaters'.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
         <a href="#cite_note-15">
          [15]
         </a>
        </sup>
        ) – spoken in the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Engadine" title="Upper Engadine">
         Upper Engadine
        </a>
        valley (
        <i>
         Engiadin' Ota
        </i>
        ) west of
        <a href="/wiki/Zernez" title="Zernez">
         Zernez
        </a>
        . Romansh was named by 5,497 people within the Upper Engadine valley (30%) as a habitually spoken language in the census of 2000.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gross31_14-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gross31-14">
          [14]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <b>
         5.
        </b>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vallader" title="Vallader">
          Vallader
         </a>
        </i>
        (rm.
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-vallader.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/44/Roh-vallader-vallader.ogg" title="Roh-vallader-vallader.ogg">
           <i>
            vallader
           </i>
          </a>
         </span>
         <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            help
           </span>
          </a>
          ·
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-vallader.ogg" title="File:Roh-vallader-vallader.ogg">
           <span style="cursor:help;">
            info
           </span>
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </span>
        ; derived from
        <i>
         val
        </i>
        'valley') – is spoken in the
        <a href="/wiki/Lower_Engadine" title="Lower Engadine">
         Lower Engadine
        </a>
        valley (
        <i>
         Engiadina Bassa
        </i>
        ) and the
        <a href="/wiki/Val_M%C3%BCstair" title="Val Müstair">
         Val Müstair
        </a>
        . It is the second most commonly spoken variety of Romansh, with 6,448 people in the Lower Engadine valley (79.2%) naming Romansh as a habitually spoken language in the census of 2000.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gross31_14-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gross31-14">
          [14]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Aside from these five major dialects, two additional varieties are often distinguished. One is the dialect of the
       <a href="/wiki/Val_M%C3%BCstair" title="Val Müstair">
        Val Müstair
       </a>
       , which is closely related to Vallader but often separately referred to as
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jauer_(Romansh)" title="Jauer (Romansh)">
         Jauer
        </a>
       </i>
       (derived from the personal pronoun
       <i>
        jau
       </i>
       'I', i.e. 'the
       <i>
        jau
       </i>
       -sayers').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curdin_1984_p._261,_265_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Curdin_1984_p._261,_265-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Less commonly distinguished is the dialect of
       <a href="/wiki/Tujetsch" title="Tujetsch">
        Tujetsch
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Val_Medel" title="Val Medel">
        Val Medel
       </a>
       , which is markedly different from Sursilvan and is referred to as
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tuatschin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tuatschin (page does not exist)">
         Tuatschin
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curdin_1984_p._261,_265_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Curdin_1984_p._261,_265-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, the standardized variety
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rumantsch_Grischun" title="Rumantsch Grischun">
        Rumantsch Grischun
       </a>
       intended for pan-regional use has been introduced since 1982. The dialect of the
       <a href="/wiki/Val_Bregaglia" title="Val Bregaglia">
        Val Bregaglia
       </a>
       is usually considered a variety of
       <a href="/wiki/Lombard_language" title="Lombard language">
        Lombard
       </a>
       and speakers use Italian as their written language, even though the dialect shares many features with the neighboring Putèr dialect of Romansh.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As these varieties form a continuum with small transitions from each village to the next, there is no straightforward internal grouping of the Romansh dialects. The Romansh language area can be described best as consisting of two widely divergent varieties, Sursilvan in the west and the dialects of the Engadine in the east, with Sutsilvan and Surmiran forming a transition zone between them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Engadinese varieties
       <i>
        Putèr
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Vallader
       </i>
       are often referred to as one specific variety known as
       <i>
        Ladin
       </i>
       (rm.
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-ladin.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/Roh-put%C3%A8r-ladin.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-ladin.ogg">
          <i>
           ladin
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-ladin.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-ladin.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ), which is not to be confused with the closely related language in Italy's
       <a href="/wiki/Dolomites" title="Dolomites">
        Dolomite mountains
       </a>
       also known as
       <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
        Ladin
       </a>
       . Sutsilvan and Surmiran are sometimes grouped together as Central Romansh (rm.
       <i>
        Grischun central
       </i>
       ), and then grouped together with Sursilvan as "Rhenish Romansh".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One feature that separates the Rhenish varieties from Ladin is the retention of the rounded front vowels
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Close_front_rounded_vowel" title="Close front rounded vowel">
         y
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front rounded vowel">
         ø
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       (written
       <i>
        ü
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        ö
       </i>
       ) in Ladin, which have been unrounded in the other dialects,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curdin_&amp;_Schläpfer1984._p._264_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Curdin_&amp;_Schläpfer1984._p._264-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as in Ladin
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-m%C3%BCr.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1e/Roh-put%C3%A8r-m%C3%BCr.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-mür.ogg">
          <i>
           mür
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-m%C3%BCr.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-mür.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       , Sursilvan
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg" title="Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg">
          <i>
           mir
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg" title="File:Roh-sursilvan-mir.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       , Surmiran
       <i>
        meir
       </i>
       ‘wall’ or Ladin
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-chasch%C3%B6l.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Roh-put%C3%A8r-chasch%C3%B6l.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-chaschöl.ogg">
          <i>
           chaschöl
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-chasch%C3%B6l.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-chaschöl.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       to Rhenish
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-caschiel.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/Roh-sursilvan-caschiel.ogg" title="Roh-sursilvan-caschiel.ogg">
          <i>
           caschiel
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-caschiel.ogg" title="File:Roh-sursilvan-caschiel.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ‘cheese’. Another is the development of Latin -CT-, which has developed into /tɕ/ in the Rhenish varieties as in
       <i>
        détg
       </i>
       ‘said’ or
       <i>
        fatg
       </i>
       ‘did’, while developing into /t/ in Ladin (
       <i>
        dit
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        fat
       </i>
       ). A feature separating Sursilvan from Central Romansh however, involves the extent of palatalization of Latin K in front of A, which is rare in Sursilvan but common in the other varieties:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curdin_&amp;_Schläpfer1984._p._264_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Curdin_&amp;_Schläpfer1984._p._264-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Sursilvan
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg" title="Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg">
          <i>
           casa
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg" title="File:Roh-sursilvan-casa.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       , Sutsilvan
       <i>
        tgea
       </i>
       , Surmiran
       <i>
        tgesa
       </i>
       , Putèr
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-chesa.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Roh-put%C3%A8r-chesa.ogg" title="Roh-putèr-chesa.ogg">
          <i>
           chesa
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-put%C3%A8r-chesa.ogg" title="File:Roh-putèr-chesa.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       , and Vallader
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg" title="Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg">
          <i>
           chasa
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg" title="File:Roh-vallader-chasa.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       'house'. Overall however, the Central Romansh varieties do not share many unique features, but rather connect Sursilvan and Ladin through a succession of numerous small dialect differences from one village to the next.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The dialects of Romansh are not always mutually comprehensible. Speakers of Sursilvan and Ladin, in particular, are usually unable to understand each other initially.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because speakers usually identify themselves primarily with their regional dialect, many do not take the effort to attempt to understand unfamiliar dialects, and prefer to speak
       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_German" title="Swiss German">
        Swiss German
       </a>
       with speakers of other varieties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A common Romansh identity is not widespread outside of intellectual circles, even though this has been changing among the younger generation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romansh_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_development_until_modern_times">
        Origins and development until modern times
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romansh_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Origins and development until modern times">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Romansh originates from the spoken Latin brought to the region by Roman soldiers, merchants, and officials following the conquest of the modern-day Grisons area by the Romans in 15 BC. Before that, the inhabitants spoke
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raetic_language" title="Raetic language">
        Raetic
       </a>
       languages, with Raetic apparently being spoken mainly in the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Engadine" title="Lower Engadine">
        Lower Engadine valley
       </a>
       . Traces of these languages survive mainly in
       <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">
        toponyms
       </a>
       , including village names such as
       <a href="/wiki/Tschlin" title="Tschlin">
        Tschlin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Scuol" title="Scuol">
        Scuol
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Savognin" title="Savognin">
        Savognin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Glion" title="Glion">
        Glion
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Breil/Brigels" title="Breil/Brigels">
        Breil/Brigels
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brienz/Brinzauls" title="Brienz/Brinzauls">
        Brienz/Brinzauls
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A4ttigau" title="Prättigau">
        Purtenza
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Trun,_Switzerland" title="Trun, Switzerland">
        Trun
       </a>
       . Additionally, a small number of pre-Latin words have survived in Romansh, mainly concerning animals, plants, and geological features unique to the
       <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">
        Alps
       </a>
       , such as
       <i>
        camutsch
       </i>
       '
       <a href="/wiki/Chamois" title="Chamois">
        chamois
       </a>
       ' and
       <i>
        grava
       </i>
       '
       <a href="/wiki/Scree" title="Scree">
        scree
       </a>
       '.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A4toromanisches_Sprachgebiet_im_Fr%C3%BChmittelalter.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="569" data-file-width="423" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/R%C3%A4toromanisches_Sprachgebiet_im_Fr%C3%BChmittelalter.PNG/220px-R%C3%A4toromanisches_Sprachgebiet_im_Fr%C3%BChmittelalter.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/R%C3%A4toromanisches_Sprachgebiet_im_Fr%C3%BChmittelalter.PNG/330px-R%C3%A4toromanisches_Sprachgebiet_im_Fr%C3%BChmittelalter.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/R%C3%A4toromanisches_Sprachgebiet_im_Fr%C3%BChmittelalter.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A4toromanisches_Sprachgebiet_im_Fr%C3%BChmittelalter.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Romansh during the early Middle Ages
         <br/>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF8000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          lost to German and Lombard, 700–1100
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF80; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Romansh-speaking area,
          <i>
           c
          </i>
          . 1100
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       It is unknown how rapidly the Celtic and Raetic inhabitants were
       <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">
        Romanized
       </a>
       following the conquest of Raetia. Some linguists assume that the area was rapidly Romanized following the Roman conquest, whereas others think that this process did not end until the 4th or 5th century, when more thoroughly Romanized Celts from farther north fled south to avoid invasions by Germanic tribes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The process was certainly complete and the pre-Roman languages extinct by the 5th–6th century, when Raetia became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom" title="Ostrogothic Kingdom">
        Ostrogothic Kingdom
       </a>
       . Around 537 AD, the Ostrogoths handed over the province of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raetia_Prima" title="Raetia Prima">
        Raetia Prima
       </a>
       to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_Empire" title="Frankish Empire">
        Frankish Empire
       </a>
       , which continued to have local rulers administering the so-called Duchy of
       <a href="/wiki/Chur" title="Chur">
        Chur
       </a>
       . However, after the death of the last
       <a href="/wiki/Victorids" title="Victorids">
        Victorid
       </a>
       ruler, Bishop
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tello,_Bishop_of_Chur" title="Tello, Bishop of Chur">
        Tello
       </a>
       , around 765,
       <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
        Charlemagne
       </a>
       assigned a Germanic duke to administer the region. Additionally, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Chur" title="Diocese of Chur">
        Diocese of Chur
       </a>
       was transferred by the Roman Catholic Church from the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Milan" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Milan">
        Archdiocese of Milan
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Mainz" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Mainz">
        Diocese of Mainz
       </a>
       in 843. The combined effect was a cultural reorientation towards the German-speaking north, especially as the ruling élite now comprised almost entirely speakers of German.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coray_2008._p._78_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Coray_2008._p._78-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the time, Romansh was spoken over a much wider area, stretching north into the present-day cantons of
       <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Glarus" title="Canton of Glarus">
        Glarus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_St._Gallen" title="Canton of St. Gallen">
        St. Gallen
       </a>
       , to the
       <a href="/wiki/Walensee" title="Walensee">
        Walensee
       </a>
       in the northwest, and
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCthi" title="Rüthi">
        Rüthi
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpine_Rhine_Valley" title="Alpine Rhine Valley">
        Alpine Rhine Valley
       </a>
       in the northeast. In the east, parts of modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Vorarlberg" title="Vorarlberg">
        Vorarlberg
       </a>
       were Romansh-speaking, as were parts of
       <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tyrol" title="County of Tyrol">
        Tyrol
       </a>
       . The northern areas, called Lower Raetia, became German-speaking by the 12th century;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and by the 15th century, the Rhine Valley of St. Gallen and the areas around the Wallensee were entirely German-speaking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coray_2008._p._78_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Coray_2008._p._78-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This language shift was a long, drawn-out process, with larger, central towns adopting German first, while the more peripheral areas around them remained Romansh-speaking longer. The shift to German was caused in particular by the influence of the local German-speaking élites and by German-speaking immigrants from the north, with the lower and rural classes retaining Romansh longer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition, beginning around 1270, the German-speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Walser" title="Walser">
        Walser
       </a>
       began settling in sparsely populated or uninhabited areas within the Romansh-speaking heartland. The Walser sometimes expanded into Romansh-speaking areas from their original settlements, which then often became German-speaking, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Davos" title="Davos">
        Davos
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schanfigg" title="Schanfigg">
        Schanfigg
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A4ttigau" title="Prättigau">
        Prättigau
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Schams" title="Schams">
        Schams
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Valendas" title="Valendas">
        Valendas
       </a>
       , which became German-speaking by the 14th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In rare cases, these Walser settlements were eventually assimilated by their Romansh-speaking neighbors, for instance,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Oberhalbstein&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Oberhalbstein (page does not exist)">
        Oberhalbstein
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Medel_(Lucmagn)" title="Medel (Lucmagn)">
        Medel
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tujetsch" title="Tujetsch">
        Tujetsch
       </a>
       in the Surselva region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1284" data-file-width="928" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg/100px-La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg/150px-La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg/200px-La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg 2x" width="100"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_mort_da_Benedetg_Fontana.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         "La mort da Benedetg Fontana", a Romansh passage in a Latin chronicle by Durich Chiampel
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Germanization of
       <a href="/wiki/Chur" title="Chur">
        Chur
       </a>
       had particular long-term consequences. Even though the city had long before ceased to be a cultural center of Romansh, the spoken language of the capital of the Diocese of Chur continued to be Romansh until the 15th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After a fire in 1465 which virtually destroyed the city, many German-speaking artisans who had been called in to help repair the damage settled there, causing German to become the majority language. In a chronicle written in 1571–72, Durich Chiampell mentions that Romansh was still spoken in Chur roughly a hundred years before, but had since then rapidly given way to German and was now not much appreciated by the inhabitants of the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coray_2008._p._78_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Coray_2008._p._78-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many linguists regard the loss of Chur to German as a crucial event. According to Sylvia Osswald, for example, it occurred precisely at a time when the introduction of the printing press could have led to the adoption of the Romansh dialect of the capital as a common written language for all Romansh speakers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other linguists such as Jachen Curdin Arquint remain skeptical of this view, however, and assume that the various Romansh-speaking regions would still have developed their own separate written standards.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Instead, several regional written varieties of Romansh began appearing during the 16th century.
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gian_Travers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gian Travers (page does not exist)">
        Gian Travers
       </a>
       wrote the first surviving work in Romansh, the
       <i>
        Chianzun dalla guerra dagl Chiaste da Müs
       </i>
       , in the Putèr dialect. This epic poem, written in 1527, describes the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musso_war" title="Musso war">
        first Musso war
       </a>
       , in which Travers himself had taken part.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liver_1999._p._95_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Liver_1999._p._95-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Travers also translated numerous biblical plays into Romansh, though only the titles survive for many of them. Another early writer,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Giachem_Bifrun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Giachem Bifrun (page does not exist)">
        Giachem Bifrun
       </a>
       , who also wrote in Putèr, penned the first printed book in Romansh, a catechism published in 1552. In 1560 he published a translation of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
        New Testament
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        L'g Nuof Sainc Testamaint da nos Signer Jesu Christ
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Two years later, in 1562, another writer from the Engadine,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Durich_Chiampel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Durich Chiampel (page does not exist)">
        Durich Chiampel
       </a>
       , published the
       <i>
        Cudesch da Psalms
       </i>
       , a collection of church songs in the Vallader dialect. These early works are generally well written and show that the authors had a large amount of Romansh vocabulary at their disposal, contrary to what one might expect of the first pieces of writing in a language. Because of this, the linguist Ricarda Liver assumes that these written works built on an earlier, pre-literature tradition of using Romansh in administrative and legal situations, of which no evidence survives.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In their prefaces, the authors themselves often mention the novelty of writing Romansh, and discuss an apparently common prejudice that Romansh was a language that could not be written.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3280" data-file-width="2071" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG/100px-Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG/150px-Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG/200px-Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG 2x" width="100"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Igl_ver_sulaz.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Front page of
         <i>
          Ilg Vêr Sulaz da pievel giuvan
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first writing in the Sursilvan and Sutsilvan dialects appears in the 17th century. As in the Engadine, these early works usually focused on religious themes, in particular the struggles between Protestants and Counter-Reformers.
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Daniel_Bonifaci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Daniel Bonifaci (page does not exist)">
        Daniel Bonifaci
       </a>
       produced the first surviving work in this category, the catechism
       <i>
        Curt mussameint dels principals punctgs della Christianevla Religiun
       </i>
       , published in 1601 in the Sutsilvan dialect. A second edition, published in 1615, is closer to Sursilvan, however, and writings in Sutsilvan do not appear again until the 20th century. In 1611,
       <i>
        Igl Vêr Sulaz da pievel giuvan
       </i>
       ("The true joys of young people"), a series of religious instructions for Protestant youths, was published by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Steffan_Gabriel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Steffan Gabriel (page does not exist)">
        Steffan Gabriel
       </a>
       . Four years later, in 1615, a Catholic catechism,
       <i>
        Curt Mussament
       </i>
       , was published in response, written by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gion_Antoni_Calvenzano&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gion Antoni Calvenzano (page does not exist)">
        Gion Antoni Calvenzano
       </a>
       . The first translation of the New Testament into Sursilvan was published in 1648 by the son of Steffan Gabriel,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luci_Gabriel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luci Gabriel (page does not exist)">
        Luci Gabriel
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The first complete translation of the Bible, the
       <i>
        Bibla da Cuera
       </i>
       , was published between 1717 and 1719. The Sursilvan dialect thus had two separate written varieties, one used by the Protestants with its cultural center around
       <a href="/wiki/Ilanz" title="Ilanz">
        Ilanz
       </a>
       , and a Catholic variety with the
       <a href="/wiki/Disentis_Abbey" title="Disentis Abbey">
        Disentis Abbey
       </a>
       as its center. The Engadine dialect was also written in two varieties: Putèr in the Upper Valley and Vallader in the Lower Valley.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Sutsilvan areas either used the Protestant variety of Sursilvan, or simply used German as their main written language. The Surmiran region began developing its own variety in the early 18th century, with a catechism being published in 1703, though either the Catholic variety of Sursilvan or Putèr was more commonly used there until the 20th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 16th century, the language border between Romansh and German largely stabilized, and it remained almost unchanged until the late 19th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Furer_2005._pp._23_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Furer_2005._pp._23-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During this period, only isolated areas became German-speaking, mainly a few villages around
       <a href="/wiki/Thusis" title="Thusis">
        Thusis
       </a>
       and the village of
       <a href="/wiki/Samnaun" title="Samnaun">
        Samnaun
       </a>
       . In the case of Samnaun, the inhabitants adopted the Bavarian dialect of neighboring Tyrol, making Samnaun the only municipality of Switzerland where a Bavarian dialect is spoken. The
       <a href="/wiki/Vinschgau" title="Vinschgau">
        Vinschgau
       </a>
       in South Tyrol was still Romansh-speaking in the 17th century, after which it became entirely German-speaking because of the
       <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">
        Counter-Reformation
       </a>
       denunciation of Romansh as a "Protestant language".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Romansh_during_the_19th_and_20th_century">
        Romansh during the 19th and 20th century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romansh_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Romansh during the 19th and 20th century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       When Grisons became part of Switzerland in 1803, it had a population of roughly 73,000, of whom around 36,600 were Romansh speakers—many of them monolingual—living mostly within the Romansh-speaking valleys.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The language border with German, which had mostly been stable since the 16th century, now began moving again as more and more villages shifted to German. One cause was the admission of Grisons as a Swiss canton, which brought Romansh-speakers into more frequent contact with German-speakers. Another factor was the increased power of the central government of Grisons, which had always used German as its administrative language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Furer_2005._pp._23_40-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Furer_2005._pp._23-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, many Romansh-speakers migrated to the larger cities, which were German-speaking, while speakers of German settled in Romansh villages. Moreover, economic changes meant that the Romansh-speaking villages, which had mostly been self-sufficient, engaged in more frequent commerce with German-speaking regions. Also, improvements in the infrastructure made travel and contact with other regions much easier than it had been.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Finally, the rise of tourism made knowledge of German an economic necessity in many areas, while the agricultural sector, which had been a traditional domain of Romansh, became less important. All this meant that knowledge of German became more and more of a necessity for Romansh speakers and that German became more and more a part of daily life. For the most part, German was seen not as a threat but rather as an important asset for communicating outside one's home region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The common people frequently demanded better access to learning German.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Furer_2005._pp._23_40-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Furer_2005._pp._23-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When public schools began to appear, many municipalities decided to adopt German as the medium of instruction, as in the case of Ilanz, where German became the language of schooling in 1833, when the town was still largely Romansh-speaking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some people even welcomed the disappearance of Romansh, in particular among progressives. In their eyes, Romansh was an obstacle to the economic and intellectual development of the Romansh people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For instance, the priest Heinrich Bansi from
       <a href="/wiki/Ardez" title="Ardez">
        Ardez
       </a>
       wrote in 1797: "The biggest obstacle to the moral and economical improvement of these regions is the language of the people, Ladin [...] The German language could certainly be introduced with ease into the Engadine, as soon as one could convince the people of the immense advantages of it".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Others however, saw Romansh as an economic asset, since it gave the Romansh an advantage when learning other Romance languages. In 1807, for example, the priest Mattli Conrad wrote an article listing the advantages and disadvantages of Romansh:
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        The Romansh language is an immense advantage in learning so much more rapidly the languages derived from Latin of France, Italy, Spain etc, as can be seen with the Romansh youth, which travels to these countries and learns their language with ease. [...] We live in between an Italian and a German people. How practical is it, when one can learn the languages of both without effort?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
         <a href="#cite_note-48">
          [48]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Mattli Conrad – 1807
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       In response however, the editor of the newspaper added that:
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        According to the testimony of experienced and vigilant language teachers, while the one who is born Romansh can easily learn to understand these languages and make himself understood in them, he has great difficulties in learning them properly, since precisely because of the similarity, he mixes them so easily with his own bastardized language. [...] in any case, the conveniences named hold no weight against all the disadvantages that come from such an isolated and uneducated language.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
         <a href="#cite_note-49">
          [49]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       According to Mathias Kundert, this quote is a good example of the attitude of many German-speakers towards Romansh at the time. According to Mathias Kundert, while there was never a plan to Germanize the Romansh areas of Grisons, many German-speaking groups wished that the entire canton would become German-speaking. They were careful however, to avoid any drastic measures to that extent, in order not to antagonize the influential Romansh minority.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The decline of Romansh over the 20th century can be seen through the results of the Swiss censuses. The decline in percentages is only partially due to the Germanization of Romansh areas, since the Romansh-speaking valleys always had a lower overall population growth than other parts of the canton.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <caption>
